=== Page 5 | TOWN OF BELMONT ===
TOWN OF BELMONT
OFFICE OF THE TOWN ADMINISTRATOR
townadministrator@belmont-ma.gov TOWN ADMINISTRATOR
455 CONCORD AVENUE PATRICE GARVIN
BELMONT, MA 02478 ASSISTANT TOWN ADMINISTRATOR
PHONE (617) 993-2610 MATHEW HASKELL
To: The Honorable Select Board
cc: Warrant Committee
cc: Residents and Taxpayers of Belmont
OVERVIEW
I herewith submit for your consideration the recommended FY2027 Operating Budget for the
Town of Belmont. I want to thank the team that assisted in the development of this budget,
Acting Finance Director Donna Tuccinardi, Fiscal Management Analyst Adrien Kordas,
Assistant Town Administrator Matt Haskell and all of the Department Heads.
Prior to discussing the FY2027 Operating Budget, it is necessary to review the chain of events
leading up to passage of the FY2025 operating budget. In April 2024, voters approved an
$8.4 million override with significant community support. While this override did not fund
many new programs or initiatives, it did play a critical role in stabilizing the Town's finances.
A portion of the override, $250,000, was allocated for capital projects such as sidewalk
improvements and other infrastructure needs. The remaining funds, however, were used to
address a growing revenue gap that had accumulated over several years.
The Town seeks to extend the override funding through FY2027 and FY2028 and anticipates
requesting another significant override in FY2029. The intent is for a successful FY2029
override to bridge the Town through FY2032, at which point the Town’s pension obligation will
have been settled. Once that obligation is resolved, additional funds are expected to be freed
within the operating budget. Please note that there has been some discussion from the
Belmont Retirement Board to extend the pension obligation further than FY2032 to fund
COLA increases for retirees.
This budget message reflects mainly on the Municipal and Shared Service pieces of the
Operating Budget. The Superintendent’s Preliminary FY2027 Operating Budget can be found
on the School website.
The two primary cost drivers in FY2027 are the facilities and health care budgets. Drivers
related to facilities are detailed in the Facilities section. Health care costs for FY2027 may be
affected by upcoming decisions regarding employee enrollment in the State’s Group
Insurance Commission (GIC).
Town Administrator's Budget Recommendation March 20, 2026
Page 1

=== Page 6 | Unknown ===
Enrollment to the GIC would begin on July 1, the change will not take effect until January 1,
2027. This creates a number of uncertainties and moving variables when estimating the total
funding required for FY2027.
For the first half of FY2027, the Town is expected to experience a 24% increase in costs under
the current plans. For the second half of the fiscal year, costs will be determined by GIC
premium rates, which introduces additional variables.
Further complicating these projections, employee behavior during the first six months of
FY2027 may shift. Employees may choose to opt in or out of coverage or select lower-cost
plans, all of which can impact overall costs.
At this time, we are using an “apples-to-apples” comparison with GIC plan structures to guide
our estimates, though this approach has limitations. These FY2027 estimates will also directly
impact projections for FY2028.
Please note that the final health insurance cost may increase or decrease based on further
review and analysis. We will continue refining these projections as more information
becomes available and as the budget is finalized.
Since my arrival in 2018, we have implemented many initiatives to increase Revenue and
create cost savings across Town government. The Town has looked to increase Revenue by
receiving grants, state appropriations, and adopting local options under Massachusetts
General Laws (MGL), to name a few. Zoning initiatives have also been passed to increase
Revenue, and the McLean development for Zones 3 and 4 will provide the Town with new
growth in the coming years. In the future, the Town will be proposing more zoning initiatives,
that will promote redevelopment and thereby enhance tax revenues for both commercial and
residential developments.
During my tenure, I have initiated the reorganization and/or restructuring of nearly every
municipal department in Town through the strategic merging of positions and the
streamlining of departmental functions, all while maintaining the quality of services provided.
I am proposing an additional restructuring within the Town Administrator’s Office and the
Cemetery Department that is expected to further improve efficiency and strengthen internal
coordination, while preserving service levels and creating the capacity to hire a Chief
Financial Officer.
These changes, driven by the need to do more with less, were a direct response to the Town’s
continued focus on tightening its belt on spending. Beginning in FY2026, the Town was able
to capitalize on the appointment of a Chief Innovation Officer, who has transformed the
Town’s IT department and infrastructure. Over the past year, the CIO has implemented
significant technology improvements, enabling the adoption of software solutions that save
time across departments and support our lean staffing model.
The Town has maintained its AAA bond rating, which has resulted in a low interest rate on
recent debt exclusions, notably the Belmont Sports Complex (BSC) and the Library, which
Town Administrator's Budget Recommendation March 20, 2026
Page 2

=== Page 7 | _________________________________________ ===
has saved a significant amount in interest expenses. The acceptance of both an appointed
Treasurer and an appointed Board of Assessors has also yielded tremendous efficiencies and
better management of the Finance Team.
All of these efforts were successful due to the leadership of the Select Board and the hard
work of the Town Departments.

The Preliminary FY2027 General Fund Operating Budget is an opportunity for some service
improvement budgeting that totals $171,673,382 and represents an increase of $2,125,298 or
1.3%, over the FY2026 budget. To support that spending, we are recommending that
$1,191,142 be withdrawn from the Override Mitigation Fund to meet overall anticipated needs
of the Town.
Budget Process and Select Board Priority - “Fiscal Rigor”
The budget process kicked off with the Select Board’s creation of the Multi-Year Budgeting
Advisory Committee (MYBAC), which began meeting in the summer of 2025 and has
continued its work to date. The committee was charged to advise the Select Board on a
multi-year budget forecast and to provide a model to help communicate and project future
overrides. As a result of this work, the Municipal Budget received a 2.7% increase for FY2027.
Town Administrator's Budget Recommendation March 20, 2026
Page 3

=== Page 8 | _________________________________________ ===
This marks the first time the Municipal Budget has seen an increase greater than 2.5% since
my arrival in 2018. The MYBAC model also shows the School Department increasing by 5.3%
in FY2027. For FY2027, the facility expenses for the Belmont Sports Complex (BSC) and the
Library have been reclassified from the Municipal Budget to the Shared Services Budget. This
represents a budgetary restructuring only and does not reflect a change in service levels or
facility operations.

*Exempt Debt Service is increasing due to the initial payment for permanent debt for the Rink and Library.
Belmont is not unlike many other municipalities that estimate revenue at the Proposition 2½
property tax levy limit and derive the majority of their property tax revenue from residential
properties. The annual budget process remains an ongoing challenge due to ever-increasing
demands on limited resources.
The lack of significant and consistent growth in property tax revenue from new growth, State
aid, and non-property tax sources, along with inflation, a tight labor market, aging
infrastructure, facilities maintenance for old and new buildings and rising health care costs,
are the primary drivers of this challenge. For FY2027, health care costs represent the most
significant budget pressure.
The FY2027 revenue estimates were reviewed at a series of Budget Summits attended by the
Select Board, School Committee, Warrant Committee and Comprehensive Capital Budget
Committee.
1. One-Time Revenue Use in Fiscal Year 2027
Free Cash is a one-time revenue source that results from the calculation, as of July 1, of a
community's remaining, unrestricted funds from its prior year operations. The Department of
Revenue annually certifies each community’s Free Cash amount based on a balance sheet
submitted as of June 30. Section C.2 of the Town’s Free Cash Policy states: “The Town will
seek to maintain Free Cash of 3-5% of the current Fiscal Year’s General Fund Revenue Budget,
with the understanding that the goal will be to maintain Free Cash of approximately 4%.” The
amount of Free Cash that is unspent in one year “carries forward” and adds to the amount
certified in the following year. Recent growth in certified Free Cash amounts is the result of
several factors and are not expected to recur.
Town Administrator's Budget Recommendation March 20, 2026
Page III-11

=== Page 16 | REVENUE ===
After considerable analysis in late 2023, Town leaders reached consensus that Free Cash has
been consistently replenished at $3,000,000 each year, which can therefore be used on an
ongoing basis to fund the budget starting in FY2025. In FY2027, this reflects 1.7% of overall
revenue. However, this comes at a risk that Free Cash may fall short of the projected
amounts, leaving a potential future shortfall. That risk is mitigated by ensuring there are
ample reserves to offset such a shortfall.
The graph below illustrates the Town’s certified Free Cash over the past 6 years. The FY2028
figure is a preliminary projection for June 30, 2026, and is subject to change based on various
factors over the next five months.

Override Mitigation Fund
In FY2026, no funds were used from the Override Mitigation Fund to balance the budget. This
will not be the case for FY2027 and FY2028, when the fund is expected to be utilized. In
FY2027, we are proposing to allocate $1,191,142 in Override Mitigation Funds to support the
operational needs of the Town. This action will result in a remaining balance of $3.2 million in
the Override Mitigation Fund for FY2028; however, this balance may be insufficient to carry
the Town through FY2028 without service reductions.

Property taxes remain the Town’s primary revenue source and the most stable source of
revenue growth, comprising 83.25% of total projected revenues in FY2027, with $142,918,458
derived from this revenue source.
Real estate and personal property tax projections include an estimate for property taxes
generated by new construction, commonly referred to as new growth. New growth is the only
way a municipality at the Proposition 2½ levy limit can generate additional property tax
revenue beyond the allowable annual increase. The Board of Assessors’ new growth estimate
for FY2027 is $900,000.
In recent years, there have been few large developments in Town. Notably, the McLean Zone
3 and Zone 4 projects will provide some new growth revenue. Additionally, one development
on Waverly, estimated at 40 units, is being counted under MGL Chapter 40A, Section 3A, a
state law provision for affordable housing. Beyond these projects, no significant
developments are currently in the pipeline, meaning new growth revenue will likely remain
limited in the coming years.

Local Receipts:
After property tax and State Aid, Local Receipts are a major source of revenue to the Town.
These revenues total $8,647,885 in FY2027, and represent 5.0% of total revenues. The main
revenue streams in this category are Motor Vehicle Excise $3,900,000, Other Excise, which
reflects both Meals and Cannabis $435,000, Ambulance Receipts $1,200,000 embedded
under Municipal Department Revenue, and Investment Income $500,000.
The Town recently adopted a local option to generate revenue from short-term rentals. The
Zoning Board of Appeals (ZBA) will be addressing short-term rentals as part of an upcoming
discussion, with the goal of providing policy guidance and establishing enforcement
procedures for short-term rental activity in Town. While revenue projections remain
conservative at this time, this initiative is expected to generate modest additional revenue
for the Town.

Municipal Services
Summary
The FY2027 budget is considered a level-service budget, but it’s important to explain what
that really means. This budget includes all required costs and some costs from prior years
that were not fully funded at the time. We are still providing the basic services residents
expect, which is why we call it level funded. However, because of limited staffing and revenue,
the quality and responsiveness of those services are not what they once were.
In past years, the Town has stayed within a 2.5% annual budget increase. FY2027 is the first
time in my eight years of preparing budgets that we have been able to plan for a 3% increase.
Looking ahead, if we return to a 2.5% increase, we will need to make changes. These may
include cutting back on overtime even further, investing in technology to help staff do more
with fewer people, and increasing certain fees, including redesigning parking fees.
The FY2027 budget for Municipal Departments is $35,098,382 which is 20.4% of the overall
recurring budget. The Municipal Services budget has increased 2.7% over FY2026. The 2.7%
Town Administrator's Budget Recommendation March 20, 2026
Page III-19

=== Page 24 | EXPENDITURES ===
increase is in line with projections made in the financial model, after moving some facilities
costs into Shared Services.
The IT Department continues to be a key focus in the FY2027 budget. Over the past year, I
have had the opportunity to begin implementing my vision for strengthening the Town’s IT
operations, and that work will continue into FY2027. The growing need for reliable IT
infrastructure in communities across Massachusetts has never been more evident.
For many years, Belmont’s IT Department was significantly underfunded, leading to outdated
technology, limited staffing, and inadequate equipment. This lack of investment created a
serious vulnerability at a time when secure and dependable IT systems are critical to daily
municipal operations and public safety.
As part of this continued investment, the Town will begin transitioning to the OpenGov
platform on July 1, starting with the Zoning and Building departments. In the years that follow,
we plan to expand OpenGov across all Town departments, creating a more efficient,
transparent, and accessible system for both staff and residents.
An overtime report was published to begin identifying the key drivers of overtime costs
across the Town. The Police and Fire Departments continue to face challenges managing
overtime due to ongoing vacancies and unplanned or uncontrolled absences. Overtime
usage has been reviewed across all departments, and reductions have been implemented in
areas where alternative funding strategies are available within existing departmental
budgets.
Below is a brief description of General Government, Public Safety, Public Services, and
Human Services. Human Services includes the newly created department of Community
Services. A more detailed budget can be found in the later pages of the preliminary budget
book.
General Government
The proposed FY2027 General Government budget is $6,455,514, which reflects an increase
from FY2026 of $387,301 and is 3.8% of the total recurring budget.
The budget increase is mainly due to higher staff costs and service expenses, especially for
the Belmont Sports Complex (BSC). The BSC currently has two full-time employees, but the
workload requires a third part-time position, which is included in this budget. This position
will be a seasonal position part-time during the rink peak season and part time during the
Community Service Departments peak season.
The cost of full-time staff for the BSC in this operating budget is $197,089. All part-time
staffing and other operating costs not covered by the Facilities budget will be paid for
through the BSC Revolving Fund. Looking ahead, the goal is to gradually reduce reliance on
the operating budget and fund more of the BSC’s expenses through the revolving fund as
revenue grows from increased rink usage.
Town Administrator's Budget Recommendation March 20, 2026
Page III-20

=== Page 25 | EXPENDITURES ===
The Town Administrator’s Office has also been restructured. At the request of the Select
Board, the Town now has a dedicated Assistant Town Administrator and a Chief Financial
Officer (CFO). This change supports succession planning and recognizes that the Town’s
budget has grown too large to be effectively managed without a CFO.
To create these two positions, the former single position was split, and the Budget Analyst
position was eliminated. As a result, only a portion of additional funding was needed, rather
than the cost of an entirely new salary.
Public Safety
The proposed FY2027 Public Safety budget is $14,825,596, an increase of $129,299 over
FY2026 and is 8.6% of the total recurring budget. The increases do not yet reflect the cost of
new collective bargaining contracts for the Police Patrol Officers and Fire Fighters unions,
whose contracts expired on June 30, 2025.
We were able to reinstate a Firefighter position that was eliminated in FY2022. This was
accomplished through a restructuring of the Parks/Cemetery Department and the
elimination of a part-time position within the Fire Department. The reinstated position will be
assigned as a daytime role within the Fire Department and will not generate overtime costs.
Reinstating the position will help keep the community safe by making sure inspections and
safety checks are done on time and done right. It would also prevent delays, reduce backlogs
when someone is out of the office, and make sure projects and code questions are handled
quickly and consistently.
Overtime in the Fire and Police Departments continues to require close monitoring.
Vacancies and employee leave create funding challenges, often causing overtime budget
lines to be overextended. While salary savings from vacant positions are used to offset a
portion of these costs, long-term retention and recruitment efforts will ultimately address
some of the underlying overtime pressures.
The Police Department’s budget was overextended in FY2025. With the hiring of a new Police
Chief, the Town anticipates strengthened oversight and improved fiscal management moving
forward. Additionally, one of the three annual scheduled police cruiser purchases has been
reduced in the FY2027 budget.
Public Services
The proposed FY2027 Public Services budget is $9,807,632, a increase of $352,175 from
FY2026, and 5.7% of the total recurring budget.
The Department of Public Works will be restructured in FY2027 with the addition of a Fields
Manager position within the Parks Division. With the implementation of the fields
maintenance contract and the new rink, the responsibilities of the Parks Manager position
were reduced to oversight of cemetery and pool operations, resulting in fewer hours needed
for that role. This shift in duties, combined with a recent administrative resignation, created
an opportunity to restructure the Parks Division while also helping to address staffing needs
at the rink and within the Fire Department.
Town Administrator's Budget Recommendation March 20, 2026
Page III-21

=== Page 26 | EXPENDITURES ===
As part of this restructuring, we are working to establish a single Operations Manager
position to oversee the Pool and Cemeteries, with expanded administrative responsibilities.
The addition of a Fields Manager position will provide much-needed expertise for the Town’s
playing fields, benefiting both municipal and school uses. This position will be partially funded
through the realignment of positions within the Parks/Cemetery Department described
above.
We continue to hear requests to hire an Economic Development Coordinator within the
Planning and Building Department. While we acknowledge these requests, we have worked
to address this need through existing staff resources and the strategic use of technology.
The Town recently added a second Planner position, which will help redistribute workload
and allow the Director to dedicate more time to economic development initiatives. In
addition, the Town will go live with OpenGov on July 1. This implementation is expected to
create efficiencies and time savings within the department, freeing up staff capacity to
support additional economic development efforts.
While an Economic Development Coordinator may be desirable, current fiscal realities and
competing demands across municipal departments require prioritization of other critical
needs at this time.
Human Services
The proposed FY2027 Human Services budget is $4,009,640, an increase of $55,232 from
FY2026, and 2.3% of the total recurring budget. The increase is due to two areas - the
opening of the new Library and an increases to the Community Services budget.
The new Library will be fully operational in FY2027. The increase in the Library budget reflects
the costs associated with operating the facility at full occupancy. These costs will need to be
closely monitored in future fiscal years. I am recommending a reduction to the Library’s
overtime line, as the Library has sufficient existing funds to cover these costs if needed.
The Library Facility budget has been formally transferred to Shared Services, which accounts
for some of the increase reflected in that section.
The Community Services Department is comprised of the Council on Aging, Recreation, and
Veterans’ Services divisions. This newly created department was formed to capitalize on staff
departures that created an opportunity to streamline operations and improve efficiency.
Shared Services
The proposed FY2027 Shared Services budget is $62,577,187 which is 36.5% of the recurring
operating budget. Shared services consists of the following:
1. Debt Service - Principal and Interest
2. Benefits: Insurance, Pension, Other Benefits (i.e. Medicare), Other Post-Employment
Benefits (OPEB)
3. Warrant Committee Reserve
4. Regional School Expenses (i.e. Vocational Education)

5. Facilities Department
6. Capital for Streets, Sidewalks, Discretionary
Debt Service - Principal and Interest
The FY2027 budget for Debt Service has increased by a net amount of $17,670 to a total of
$17,698,826 due to the new in-levy debt policy. Exempt debt for FY2027 is $16,648,826, or
9.7% of the recurring budget, while within levy debt service is $1,050,000, or 0.6% of the
recurring budget. The Exempt Debt total includes the Rink, Library and Belmont Middle and
High School projects. Table 9 reflects overall debt services obligations of the Town, including
Water and Sewer Enterprise.

Benefits - Insurance, Pension, Other Benefits, and OPEB
Benefits include Pension, Retiree and Employee Health Insurance, Medicare, Workers’
Compensation, Unemployment and OPEB. The FY2027 proposed budget for the category is
$29,670,322, an increase of $2,732,576, or 10.14%, and represents a transition year for health
insurance rates. Now that we are moving past the pandemic, employees are reengaging with
their healthcare providers, causing claims to increase.
In 2020, at the onset of the COVID-19 pandemic, we made the strategic decision to
implement a baseline annual increase of 3% for health insurance costs. This proactive
approach proved beneficial, as reduced medical visits and claims during the first three years
of the pandemic temporarily lowered overall healthcare expenditures.
By maintaining moderate, consistent rate increases during that period, we were able to
lessen the impact of significantly larger cost adjustments in FY2025 and FY2026 for both
employees and the Town. In addition, for FY2025 and FY2026, we relied on the strong balance
of the Health Insurance Trust to help keep rates lower than they otherwise would have been.
However, as healthcare utilization has rebounded post-pandemic, claims began rising in
FY2025; one of the largest factors is the introduction of GLP1s into the market. This increase
has led to a substantial drawdown of the Health Insurance Trust. As a result, the Trust cannot
be relied upon to offset rate increases for FY2027, which has contributed to a significant
spike in projected rates.
Health insurance currently represents approximately eleven percent (11%) of the Town’s
operating budget, which necessitates the Town’s transition to the Massachusetts Group
Town Administrator's Budget Recommendation March 20, 2026
Page III-23

=== Page 28 | Debt Service - Principal and Interest ===
Insurance Commission (GIC). This transition is intended to generate savings and reduce
costs for both the Town and its employees.
For FY2027, pension costs are projected to resume a more moderate level of increase of
$253,207 or 2.5%, which is projected to reach full-funding in 2032. The Retirement Board is
considering extending the pension liability funding schedule beyond FY2032. As of the writing
of this message, a final decision has not yet been made.
Property and Liability Insurance and Workers’ Compensation premium costs are estimated to
increase by a combined $75,502 or approximately 5.7%, with increases in both areas driven
by a volatile insurance marketplace offset by decreases to Workers’ Compensation to
capture some savings due to lower spending levels in recent years. It is important to note
that the General Liability of the new BSC and Library have increased over the prior years due
to the new construction.
Other post-employment benefits (OPEB) are the life and health insurance benefits that
employees become eligible for once they retire. The assets of an OPEB trust are held solely
to meet the current and future liabilities for group health insurance benefits for retirees and
their dependents, and are subject to appropriation. Table 10 shows the OPEB contributions
each year since FY2022.

Regional Schools (Vocational Education)
The FY2027 Regional School expense is estimated at $327,917, an increase of $93,338. The
increase is attributable to newly available enrollment openings at Minuteman Regional
School, an option that was not previously accessible to Belmont students.
Facilities Department
We are proposing an increase of $827,760 in the Facilities budget. This increase is due to
contractual obligations under a new collective bargaining agreement, anticipated increases
in service contracts, the addition of a new full-time employee to support building
maintenance, and the addition of the BSC and the Library.
Since 2018, we have steadily built out the Facilities Department to support both the Town and
the Schools. During this period, several debt exclusions for new construction projects have
significantly increased the Town’s building square footage and introduced more advanced
building systems requiring specialized maintenance.
Town Administrator's Budget Recommendation March 20, 2026
Page III-24

=== Page 29 | Debt Service - Principal and Interest ===
In the fall of 2025, two additional buildings came online and will now require ongoing
maintenance and operational support. Given this continued expansion, it is critical that
appropriate funding be allocated to ensure these facilities are properly maintained.
In addition, both the BSC and the Library have been fully electrified. Combined with the
added square footage, this transition has contributed to increased utility costs. However,
these impacts will be partially offset by savings generated from the solar arrays installed on
the buildings’ roofs.
Finally, we have added a position within the Facilities Department. With the addition of new
buildings, increasingly complex building systems, and the completion of a comprehensive
facilities assessment, there is a clear and demonstrated need for an additional full-time
employee to support both our existing infrastructure and the newly operational facilities.
Capital Budget
The FY2027 Capital Budget contains $2,080,376 to support capital projects which will be
recommended by the Comprehensive Capital Budget Committee (CCBC), and represents
2.7% of the General Fund recurring operating budget.
The amount dedicated to Capital includes $1.95M in the traditional budget allocation. A more
detailed Capital Budget will be released once the CCBC completes its recommendations for
FY2027.
Capital Budget - Roads and Sidewalks
The FY2027 Budget contains $2,050,632 million to support the ongoing Pavement
Management Program which funds roadway reconstruction in Belmont. This amount is in
addition to approximately $793,644, which is received annually from State Chapter 90
Highway Funds.
The FY2027 Budget contains $525,065 to support sidewalk repair, which grows by 2.5% each
year in line with Proposition 2½. This includes $250,000 from the 2024 Override that could be
reallocated in future years to other capital needs.
School Department
The attached School Department budget of $73,997,814 reflects an increase of $3,379,195
from FY2026 or 4.8%, and is 43.1% of the overall recurring budget. In addition to the direct
appropriations noted, an additional $12,799,672 is budgeted for School Benefits in Shared
Services to reflect the benefits costs for School staff. Please see the Superintendent’s budget
for details on how the school and shared services budgets account for the 5.3% increase in
the FY2027 schools budget reported in the MYBAC model.

Additional Comments
Enterprise Funds: Water/Sewer & Stormwater
The FY2027 Enterprise budgets are included within the Department of Public Works.
However, it is noteworthy that the Town has not yet received initial estimates for the MWRA
Assessments, which are the largest parts of both the Water and Sewer enterprise budgets.
Placeholder increases of 5% have been included. Initial estimates are typically received in
mid-February; the final budget recommendation will reflect the updated assessments.
Per a recent discussion with the Select Board, we are planning to introduce a warrant article
to create a Stormwater Enterprise Fund at the 2026 fall town meeting , which would be part
of the annual budget beginning in FY2028. This would be an important step toward improving
transparency and understanding of costs associated with stormwater management. The
creation of a Stormwater Enterprise Fund would allow the Town to better track, manage, and
fund its stormwater management operations in a more organized and transparent manner.
This move aims to provide clear financial information about the costs and revenue
associated with managing stormwater, making it easier for residents and stakeholders to
understand how fees are applied and how funds are utilized.
Reserve Balances:
The reserve ratio as of the end of FY2025 is 13.6% of the General Fund budget. Table 11
reflects the balances of the Town’s reserves as of June 30, 2025, including carryforward Free
Cash.

Revenue Executive Summary
Town of Belmont, MA
This revenue projection is based on the most current data available; as new information
arises, the projections may be revised. The summary below presents Total General Fund
Operating Revenues, and Net General Fund Revenues.
• Total General Fund Operating Revenues are from annually recurring and non-recurring
revenue sources, including transfers from special revenue funds, and Specialized
Stabilization Funds.
• Net General Fund Revenues are Total General Fund Revenues less revenues
recommended to be set-aside to fund designated expenses.
In FY2027, Total General Fund Operating Revenues are projected to increase by
approximately $2.13 million, or 1.25%. Net General Fund Revenues, those available to support
school and municipal operating budgets, are projected to increase by $8.02 million, or 5.04%.

Detailed Description:
Property Tax Levy: The FY2027 property tax levy is projected to increase approximately $3.96
million, or 3.2%. The projected levy is a function of the FY2026 levy limit increased by 2.5% per
Proposition 2½, plus an increment for new growth. FY2027 new growth will be a function of
construction activity for the period January 1, 2025 to December 31, 2025. FY2027 new
growth is projected at $900,000 based on a review of historical new growth data and
recommendations from the Board of Assessors.
Tax Levy - Exempt Debt: When voters approve a debt exclusion for a capital project, the debt
service for those projects is tracked separately from the base tax levy. For FY2027, debt
service is projected to increase by $0.06 million or 0.36%, due to the first payments on
permanent debt issued for the new library and skating rink.
State Aid: An overall State Aid increase of $632,102 or 3.99% is projected for FY2027, which
reflects the initial figures included in the MYBAC model and not the Governor’s budget
released on January 22, 2026. The Town is awaiting action on the House budget to determine
whether additional net state aid will be approved prior to Annual Town Meeting (ATM). Final
figures are likely to be known in late June 2026 when the Legislature adopts, and the
Governor signs, the FY2027 State budget.

=== Page 34 | Revenue Executive Summary ===
Revenue Executive Summary
Town of Belmont, MA
Local Receipts: FY2027 projections for each category of receipt are based on the history of
actual collections and projections of 3- and 5-year historical averages. Main areas for
adjustment include -
• Investment Income has benefited from interest rate increases since mid-2022. For
FY2027, interest income is projected, but is limited to $500,000, which is a level that is
deemed recurring. Any excess revenue received above this level should be used for
one-time expenses.
• Higher-than-average building permit revenue is projected for FY2026 and FY2027 as a
result of the two McLean projects in Zone 3 and Zone 4. The resulting increase will be
incorporated into Free Cash totals and should be treated as one-time revenue to
support one-time expenditures.
Available Funds: Recurring Free Cash of $3,000,000 is being used for both the operating
budget and Other Post-Employment Benefits (OPEB).
An additional $1,000,000 in Free Cash was also used to offset the health insurance increase,
given the exceptionally high rate adjustment.
Revenue Offsets: Revenue Offsets are projected to increase by approximately $45,009 or
1.46%. Revenue Offsets represent the set-aside of a portion of projected revenues legally
required for particular purposes, including:
(1) cherry sheet assessments - estimated charges to be levied by the Commonwealth to
cover the costs of state and regional services provided to the Town, based on
preliminary state budget information; and
(2) the Assessor's Overlay account which covers the cost of abatements and
exemptions granted to property taxpayers.
Enterprise Receipts: This category of revenue represents transfers from the Water and
Sewer Enterprise Funds and the Belmont Municipal Light Department to the General Fund to
cover General Fund expenditures that support the operations of the water, sewer and light
departments. Beginning in FY2024, Finance staff conducted an annual detailed review of the
water and sewer indirect charges which resulted in a decrease in indirect transfers, which
were mostly offset by water and sewer making higher direct contributions for other budget
items.

=== Page 37 | Program: General Government ===
Program: General Government
1100 Board of Assessors
Town of Belmont, MA
Program Overview
The Board of Assessors is required by Massachusetts New Growth
General Law to list and value all real and personal property. Any change in value due to property enhancements is
considered new growth and increases the Tax Levy above
Assessors are required to submit these values to the State the annual 2.5% limit. The Assessors’ Office collects
Department of Revenue (DOR) for certification every five building permit information from the Office of Planning and
years. The last recertification was in FY2025. In the years Building. Each property is reviewed, inspected and adjusted

1400 Town Accountant
Town of Belmont, MA
Program Overview
The Town Accountant (TA) maintains fiscal records and Accounts Payable
internal controls for all Town and School departments. The The TA manages vendor setup, reviews invoices processed
department ensures that all financial reporting by all departments, handles department and vendor
requirements are completed in accordance with federal and requests and questions, and certifies availability of funds
state laws and Town Bylaws. prior to signing contracts and paying invoices.
Accounting Reporting
The TA prepares and maintains key financial records for all The TA coordinates with Human Resources, Retirement,
funds, including General Ledger and Financial Statements. Schools and Treasurer to prepare data for the biennial
The TA submits Balance Sheets for Free Cash Certification actuarial studies for the Retirement System and for Other
and Schedule A, and assists in the submission of Tax Recap Post-Employment Benefits (OPEB).
sheets to Department of Revenue for certification of the
annual Tax Rate. Other - Committees
The Town Accountant is an ex-officio member of the
Auditing Permanent Audit Committee and the Retirement Board.
The TA works with external auditors to present the annual
audited financial statements in conformity with GAAP and
GASB. The TA regularly audits health insurance, salary and
other benefits expenses. The Department reviews internal
procedures of all departments and performs fraud risk
assessments.

Program Overview
The Town Clerk’s Office secures records and communicates Elections & Registrations
governmental information in a timely manner. In addition, Responsible for all aspects of elections and managing the
the Town Clerk’s office runs all of the elections, manages Town census of voters and residents in compliance with
the list of voters and residents and fully supports Town local, state and federal laws. Works with the Board of
Meeting, Belmont’s legislative body. Registrars of Voters. Verify residency for inquiring agencies.
Town Clerk Legislative
Responsible for creating, registering and maintaining Responsible for managing Town Meeting, its preparation
official Town records, including births, deaths, marriages, and operations, with the elected Moderator; submitting
Town Meeting votes and transcripts, business licenses and votes as required to the Attorney General, Department of
business certificates (d/b/a), pet licenses, legal postings of Revenue and other State agencies, coordinating logistics
meetings and filings and appointment of committees and for Town Meeting with the Moderator and Town staff,
governmental bodies. The Town Clerk is also the Town’s maintaining contact information for and performing official
Public Records Officer, and central point of information and communications to Town Meeting Members by email.
records of Ethics, the Open Meeting Law and Campaign
Finance Laws.

Program Overview
Included in the Employee Benefits and Insurance program Unemployment Compensation:
are costs for the Town’s pension assessment, workers’ The cost of unemployment payments for eligible employees
compensation, unemployment insurance, health and life separated from Municipal or School Department
insurance benefits and Medicare. employment. The Town self-insures for this expense.
Contributory Retirement Assessment: Workers’ Compensation:
The assessment of the Belmont Contributory Retirement The insurance premiums to cover Municipal and School
System levied to the Town to finance a portion of employees injured on the job.
retirement benefits of Town and non-teaching School
employees. This assessment is issued pursuant to Property and Liability Insurance:
Massachusetts General Laws (MGL) Chapter 32 and is The cost of premiums for policies that: (1) protect the Town
based on an actuarial valuation of the funding obligations of against property loss and damage; (2) insure the Town’s
the Belmont Contributory Retirement System. In addition to vehicles; and (3) cover the Town against liability claims.
this assessment, employee contributions - ranging from 8%
to 11% depending on date of hire - provide the majority of Deductible Reserves:
pension system funding. Covers uninsured property losses, settlements and
deductibles contained in various insurance policies.
Employee/Retiree Benefits:
The Town’s annual contribution for health and life insurance
for active Municipal and School Department employees and
retirees, and the Town’s 1.45% share of Medicare tax for all
employees hired after 1986.
FY2025-26 Achievements
• Staff have developed a more streamlined process for the
monthly reconciliation of benefits and bill payments.
• In addition, a model for forecasting health benefits was
developed using a snapshot of enrollees, a placeholder
for vacancies, and a small assumption for enrollment
changes.

Program Overview
The Office of Planning and Building has two divisions with the following primary responsibilities:
Planning Division Building and Inspection Services Division
Handles land use, economic development, zoning, and Performs building code duties including permit reviews and
other planning issues for the Town. The Division provides inspections and project reviews for zoning compliance. This
professional “in-house” planning services, project-related division also enforces local zoning and general By-Laws, as
services including review and discussions of preliminary well as state codes and regulations such as accessibility
and final development plans; staff to support permanent regulations. Much of what this division does is mandated by
and temporary committees; and public services through state law.

owners and other interested parties.

=== Page 220 | APPENDIX A - GLOSSARY OF KEY TERMS ===
APPENDIX A - GLOSSARY OF KEY TERMS
Abatement - A complete or partial cancellation of a tax levy imposed by a governmental unit
as administered by the local Board of Assessors.
Accounting System - A system of financial recordkeeping which records, classifies, and
reports information on the financial status and operation of an organization.
Accrual Basis - The basis of accounting under which transactions are recognized when they
occur, regardless of the timing of related cash flows.
Adopted Budget - The resulting budget approved by Town Meeting.
Advance Refunding Bonds - Bonds issued to refund an outstanding bond issue prior to the
date on which the outstanding bonds become due or callable. Proceeds of the advance
refunding bonds are deposited in escrow with a fiduciary, invested in U.S. Treasury Bonds or
other authorized securities, and used to redeem the underlying bonds at maturity or call date
and to pay interest on the bonds being refunded or the advance refunding bonds.
Allocation - The distribution of available monies, personnel, buildings and equipment among
various Town departments, divisions or cost centers.
Annual Budget - Estimate of expenditures for specific purposes during the fiscal year (July 1 -
June 30) and the proposed means for financing those activities using revenues.
Appropriation - An authorization by the Town to make obligations and payments from the
treasury for a specific purpose.
Arbitrage - Investing funds borrowed at a lower interest cost in investments providing a
higher rate of return.
Assessed Valuation - A valuation set upon real or personal property by the board of
assessors as a basis for levying taxes.
Audit - A study of the Town’s accounting system to ensure that financial records are
accurate and in compliance with all legal requirements for handling of public funds, including
state law and city charter.
Availability - Available Square Feet divided by the Net Rentable Area.
Balanced Budget - A budget in which receipts are greater than (or equal to) expenditures
required by statute for all Massachusetts cities and towns. A balanced budget is a basic
budgetary constraint intended to ensure that a government does not spend beyond its
means and its use of resources for operating purposes does not exceed available resources
over a defined budget period.
Town Administrator's Budget Recommendation March 20, 2026
Page XI-216

=== Page 221 | Town of Belmont, MA ===
Basis of Accounting - Basis of accounting refers to when revenues and expenditures or
expenses are recognized in accounts and reported on financial statements. Basis of
accounting relates to the timing of the measurements made, regardless of the measurement
focus applied.
Bond - A written promise to pay a specified sum of money, called the face value (par value) or
principal amount, at a specified date or dates in the future, called maturity date(s), together
with periodic interest at a specified rate. The difference between a note and a bond is that
the latter runs for a longer period of time.
Bond Anticipation Notes - Notes issued in anticipation of later issuance of bonds, usually
payable from the proceeds of the sale of the bonds or of renewal notes.
Bonds Authorized and Unissued - Bonds that a government has been authorized to sell but
has not sold. Issuance at this point is only contingent upon action by the treasurer.
Bond Counsel - An attorney or law firm engaged to review and submit an opinion on the legal
aspects of a municipal bond or note issue.
Bond Issue - The sale of a certain number of bonds at one time by a governmental unit.
Budget (Operating) – The operating budget is a plan of financial operation including an
estimate of proposed expenditures for a defined period and the proposed means of financing
expenditures.
Budget Basis of Accounting - The Town’s General Fund budget is prepared on a basis other
than generally accepted accounting principles (GAAP). The actual results of operations are
presented on a “budget (cash) basis” to provide a meaningful comparison of actual results
with the budget.
Budget Calendar - The schedule of key dates or milestones a government follows in the
preparation and adoption of the budget.
Budget Message - A general discussion of the submitted budget presented in writing by the
Town Administrator as part of the budget document.
Capital Budget - The Capital Budget is a plan of proposed outlays for acquiring long-term
assets and the means of financing those acquisitions during the current fiscal period.
Capital Expenditures - Expenditures which result in the acquisition or addition to fixed
assets.
Capital Improvements Program - A comprehensive schedule for planning a community’s
capital expenditures. It coordinates community planning, fiscal capacity and physical
development. While all of a community’s needs should be identified in the program, there
should also be a set of criteria that prioritizes expenditures. A capital program is a plan for
capital expenditures that extends four years beyond the capital budget and is updated yearly.
Town Administrator's Budget Recommendation March 20, 2026
Page XI-217

=== Page 222 | Town of Belmont, MA ===
Cash Basis of Accounting - Revenues recorded when cash is received and expenses are
recognized when cash is paid out.
Charges for Service - (Also called User Charges or Fees) The charges levied on the users of
particular goods or services provided by local government, requiring individuals to pay for the
private benefits they receive. Such charges reduce the reliance on property tax funding.
Cherry Sheet - A form showing all state charges and reimbursements distributed to the Town
as certified by the state director of accounts. Years ago this document was printed on cherry
colored paper.
Community Preservation Act - On November 2, 2010, residents of Belmont accepted the
Community Preservation Act (CPA) which allows the Town to impose a surcharge of 1.5% on
real estate taxes. Property exempt from this tax includes the first $100,000 of residential
property as well as certain low-income properties. By enacting the CPA, the Town will receive
the maximum available matching funds from the state. Proceeds from both the amount
raised by the Town and the amount matched by the State will be used to fund renovations to,
and the construction of affordable housing, open space acquisition and historic preservation.
Cost-Benefit Analysis – A decision-making tool that allows a comparison of options based on
the level of benefit derived and the cost incurred for each different alternative.
Cost Center - The lowest hierarchical level of allocating monies, often referred to as a
program, project or operation.
Debt Authorization - Formal approval to incur debt by municipal officials, in accordance with
procedures stated in M.G.L. Ch. 44, specifically sections 2, 3, 4 and 6 through 15.
Debt Burden - The debt burden is the level of debt of an issuer, usually as compared to a
measure of value (debt as a percentage of assessed value, debt per capita, etc.). Sometimes
debt burden is used in referring to debt service costs as a percentage of the annual budget.
Debt Limits - The general debt limit of a city or town consists of the normal debt limit, which
is 5% of the valuation of taxable property and a double debt limit, which is 10% of that
valuation. Cities and towns may authorize debt up to the normal limit without state approval,
while debt up to the double debt limit requires state approval. It should be noted that there
are certain categories of debt which are exempt from these limits.
Debt Service - Payment of interest and repayment of principal to holders of a government’s
debt instruments.
Deficit or Budget Deficit - The deficit or budget deficit occurs when there is an excess of
budget expenditures over receipts/revenues. The city charter requires a balanced budget.
Department - A principal, functional and administrative entity created by statute and/or the
Select Board to carry out specified public services.
Town Administrator's Budget Recommendation March 20, 2026
Page XI-218

=== Page 223 | Town of Belmont, MA ===
Departmental Accomplishments - Completion of a goal or activity that warrants
announcement by one or more department.
Encumbrance - Obligations in the form of purchase orders and contracts which are
chargeable to an appropriation and are reserved. They cease to be encumbrances when paid
or when an actual liability is set up.
Enterprise Fund - A fund established to account for operations that are financed and
operated in a manner similar to private business enterprises. The intent is that the full cost of
providing the goods or services be financed primarily through charges and fees thus
removing the expenses from the tax rate.
Equalized Valuations - (EQVs) The determination of the full and fair cash value of all property
in the Commonwealth that is subject to local taxation. EQVs have historically been used as
variables in distributing certain state aid accounts, and for determining county assessments
and certain other costs. The Commissioner of Revenue, in accordance with M.G.L. Ch. 58, s.
10C, is charged with the responsibility of biennially determining an equalized valuation for
each town and city in the Commonwealth.
Excess Levy Capacity - The difference between the levy limit and the amount of real and
personal property taxes actually levied in a given year. Annually, the Select Board must be
informed of excess levying capacity and evidence of their acknowledgement must be
submitted to DOR when setting the tax rate.
Expenditures - The amount of money, cash or checks actually paid or obligated for payment
from the treasury.
Fiduciary Fund - Repository of money held by a municipality in a trustee capacity or as an
agent for individuals, private organizations, other governmental units and other funds. These
include expendable trusts, non-expendable trusts, pension trusts and other agency funds.
Financing Plan - The estimate of revenues and their sources that will pay for the service
programs outlined in the annual budget.
Financial Task Force – FTF – The Task Force was formed by the Select Board to develop a
long term financial and capital plan.
Fiscal Year - The twelve month financial period used by all Massachusetts municipalities,
beginning July 1 and ending June 30 of the following calendar year. The fiscal year is identified
by the year in which it ends.
Free Cash - (Also Budgetary Fund Balance) Funds remaining from the operations of the
previous fiscal year which are certified by DOR’s director of accounts as available for
appropriation. Remaining funds include unexpended free cash from the previous year,
receipts in excess of estimates shown on the tax recapitulation sheet and unspent amounts
Town Administrator's Budget Recommendation March 20, 2026
Page XI-219

=== Page 224 | Town of Belmont, MA ===
in budget line-items. Unpaid property taxes and certain deficits reduce the amount of
remaining funds which can be certified as free cash.
Full and Fair Market Valuation - The requirement, by State law, that all real and personal
property be assessed at 100% of market value for taxation purposes. “Proposition 2½” laws
set the Town’s tax levy limit at 2½% of the full market (assessed) value of all taxable property.
Fund - A set of interrelated accounts which record assets and liabilities related to a specific
purpose. Also a sum of money available for specified purposes.
Fund Accounting - Governmental accounting systems should be organized and operated on
a fund basis. A fund is defined as a fiscal and accounting entity with a self-balancing set of
accounts recording cash and other financial resources, together with all related liabilities and
residual equities or balances, and changes therein, which are segregated for the purpose of
carrying on specific activities or attaining certain objectives in accordance with special
regulations, restrictions or limitations.
Fund Balance - The excess of assets of a fund over its liabilities and reserves.
GASB 34 - A major pronouncement of the Governmental Accounting Standards Board
(GASB) requires a report on overall financial health, including trends, prospects for the future,
cost of delivering services and value estimates on public infrastructure assets.
General Fund - The major municipality-owned fund, which is created with City receipts and
which is charged with expenditures payable from such revenues.
Generally Accepted Accounting Principles (GAAP) - A set of uniform accounting and
financial reporting rules and procedures that define accepted accounting practice.
General Obligation Bonds - Bonds issued by a municipality which are backed by the full faith
and credit of its taxing authority.
Geographical Information System (GIS) - Computerized mapping system and analytical tool
that allows a community to raise and sort information on a parcel, area or community wide
basis.
Goal - A proposed course of action toward which departmental effort is directed.
Governmental Funds - Funds generally used to account for tax-supported activities. There
are five different types of governmental funds: the general fund, special revenue funds, debt
service funds, capital projects funds and permanent funds.
Grant - A contribution of assets by one governmental unit or other organization to another.
Typically, these contributions are made to local governments from the state and federal
government. Grants are usually made for specific purposes.
Town Administrator's Budget Recommendation March 20, 2026
Page XI-220

=== Page 225 | Town of Belmont, MA ===
Hotel/Motel Excise - Allows a community to assess a tax on short-term room occupancy at
hotels, motels and lodging houses, as well as convention centers in selected cities.
Interest - Compensation paid or to be paid for the use of money, including interest payable at
periodic intervals or as a discount at the time a loan is made.
Interfund Transactions. Payments from one administrative budget fund to another or from
one trust fund to another, which results in the recording of a receipt and an expenditure.
Intrafund Transactions - Financial transactions between activities within the same fund, an
example would be a budget transfer.
License and Permit Fees - The charges related to regulatory activities and privileges granted
by government as defined in bylaw and regulation.
Levy Limit - The maximum amount of tax a community can levy in a given year. The limit can
grow each year by 2.5 percent of the prior year’s levy limit (M.G.L. Ch. 59, s. 21C (f,g,k)), plus
new growth and any overrides. The levy limit can exceed the levy ceiling only if the
community passes a capital expenditure exclusion, debt exclusion or special exclusion.
Line-Item Budget - A format of budgeting which organizes costs by type of expenditure such
as supplies, equipment, maintenance or salaries.
Massachusetts Water Pollution Abatement Trust (MWPAT) - A statewide revolving fund
that commenced operations in 1990 to address necessary environmental actions outlined in
the Federal Clean Water Act. This fund revolves by the MWPAT issuing large pooled bond
issues for various environmental construction projects and then loaning these funds to
communities, with subsidies from the state reducing the debt service payments for these
communities.
Meals Excise - Local excise option which allows communities to assess a sales tax on sales of
restaurant meals originating in the city by a vendor.
Modified Accrual Basis - The accrual basis of accounting adapted to the governmental fund
type, wherein only current assets and current liabilities are generally reported on fund
balance sheets and the fund operating statements present financial flow information
(revenues and expenditures). Revenues are recognized when they become both measurable
and available to finance expenditures in the current period. Expenditures are recognized
when the related fund liability is incurred, except for a few specific exceptions. All
governmental funds and expendable trust funds are accounted for using the modified
accrual basis of accounting.
N/A - The information is not available or not applicable.
Non-Tax Revenue - All revenue coming from non-tax sources including licenses and permits,
intergovernmental revenue, charges for service, fines and forfeits and other miscellaneous
revenue.
Town Administrator's Budget Recommendation March 20, 2026
Page XI-221

=== Page 226 | Town of Belmont, MA ===
Official Statement - A document prepared for potential investors containing information
about a prospective bond or note issue and the issuer.
Overlay - The amount raised by the assessors in excess of appropriations and other charges
for the purpose of creating a fund to cover abatements and exemptions.
Pay-As-You-Go Funds - The appropriation of current revenues, including Property Taxes and
Free Cash, to fund capital improvements, as opposed to incurring debt to cover the costs.
Policy - A definite course of action adopted after a review of information, and directed at the
realization of goals.
Procedure - A method used in carrying out a policy or plan of action.
Program - Collections of work-related activities initiated to accomplish a desired end.
Program Budget - A budget format which organizes expenditures and revenues around the
type of activity or service provided and specifies the extent or scope of service to be
provided, stated whenever possible in precise units of measure.
Proposition 2½ - A statewide tax limitation initiative petition limiting the property tax levy in
cities and towns in the Commonwealth to 2½ percent of the full and fair cash valuation of the
taxable real and personal property in that city or town. The statute also places an annual
growth cap of 2½ percent on the increase in the property tax levy.
Purchase Order - A document issued to authorize a vendor or vendors to deliver specified
merchandise or render a specified service for a stated or estimated price. Outstanding
purchase orders are called encumbrances.
Purpose & Overview - A short description of a Town department or division describing the
charges and/or functions of that particular department or division.
Rating Agencies - This term usually refers to Moody’s Investors Service, Standard and Poor’s
Corporation and Fitch Ratings. These are the three major agencies that issue credit ratings
on municipal bonds.
Refunding Bonds - Retirement of an existing bond issue through the sale of a new bond issue
when interest rates have fallen, issuers may want to exercise the call feature of a bond and
replace it with another debt instrument paying a lower interest rate.
Registered Bonds - Bonds registered on the books of the issuer as to ownership; the transfer
of ownership must also be recorded on the books of the issuer. Recent changes in federal tax
laws mandate that all municipal bonds be registered if their tax exempt status is to be
retained.
Town Administrator's Budget Recommendation March 20, 2026
Page XI-222

=== Page 227 | Town of Belmont, MA ===
Reserves - An account used to indicate that portion of fund equity which is legally restricted
for a specific purpose or not available for appropriation and subsequent spending.
Reserve for Contingencies - A budgetary reserve set aside for emergencies or unforeseen
expenditures not otherwise budgeted.
Revaluation - A reasonable and realistic program to achieve the fair cash valuation of
property, in order to ensure that each taxpayer in the community pays his or her share of the
cost of local government in proportion to the value of their property.
Revenue - Additions to the Town’s financial assets (such as taxes and grants) which do not in
themselves increase the Town’s liabilities or cancel out a previous expenditure. Revenue may
also be created by cancelling liabilities, provided there is no corresponding decrease in
assets or increase in other liabilities.
Revolving Fund - A fund established to finance a continuing cycle of operations in which
receipts are available for expenditure without further action by Town Meeting.
Service Level - The extent or scope of the Town’s service to be provided in a given budget
year. Whenever possible, service levels should be stated in precise units of measure.
Service Program - A planned agenda for providing benefit to citizens.
Significant Budget Modification - An increase or decrease of a departmental budget of such
importance that highlighting is necessary.
Submitted Budget - The proposed budget approved by the Select Board and forwarded to
Town Meeting for their approval. The Council must act upon the submitted budget within
prescribed guidelines and limitations according to statute and the Town charter.
Supplemental Appropriations - Appropriations made by Town Meeting after an initial
appropriation, to cover expenditures beyond original estimates.
Tax Anticipation Notes - Notes issued in anticipation of taxes, which are usually retired from
taxes collected.
Tax Rate - The amount of tax levy stated per $1,000 in value of the tax base. Prior to a 1978
amendment to the Massachusetts Constitution, a single tax rate applied to all of the taxable
real and personal property in a city or town. The 1978 amendment allowed the legislature to
create three classes of taxable property: 1) residential real property, 2) open space land, and
3) all other (commercial, industrial and personal) property, each of which may be taxed at a
different rate. Within limits, cities and towns are given the option of determining the share of
the levy to be borne by the different classes of property. The share borne by residential real
property must be at least 65% of the full rate. The share of commercial, industrial and
personal property must not exceed 175% of the full rate. Property may not be classified until
the state department of revenue has certified that all property has been assessed at its full
value.

Unrestricted General Government Aid (UGGA) - The components of local aid including
additional assistance and lottery aid, which were combined into this one category, UGGA.
Valuation (100%) - A requirement that the assessed valuation must be the same as the
market value for all properties.
